рдЕрде рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ тАШ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕рджрд╛рдкреГрдгреЛ рдирд╛рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдп рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рдЫрдиреНрджрдГ ред ’ рд╡реИ рддрддреН ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рджрдордкрд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рд╡рд┐рджрд╛ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢ рд╕рджрд╛рдкреГрдгрдГ ред рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

45 (399)
All Gods
Sad─Бpr╠ес╣Зa ─Аtreya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A lovely hymn, both narrating the opening of the Vala cave by the power of the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ poetic speech and welcoming the dawn of a new day and the sunrise on that mythic model. The hymn begins (vss. 1тАУ3) with a description of sunrise, with no overt mention of the myth, though it clearly lurks in the background. The poet is concerned to apply the mythic model to the current sacrificial situation. He initiates the ritual in verse 4, and then in the two, paired, middle verses in the hymn (5тАУ6), an omphalos, he exhorts his priestly comrades to achieve the poetic vision (dh─л╠Б) that has served others well in the past. The particular past he has in mind becomes clear in the following two verses (7тАУ8), which depict the opening of the Vala cave and the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ role in it. The next two verses first pray that the Sun will come up (9) and then announce that he has arisen (10). The exhortations in verses 5тАУ6 have worked! In the last verse (11) the poet (addressing himself, as well as his priestly colleagues) exults over this success: тАЬthe poetic vision that wins the sun,тАЭ the same one that the Aс╣Еgirases possessed, has now been acquired, and it will bring welfare to the community. It is noteworthy that Indra, the usual hero of the Vala myth, is not mentioned in connection with it (though he does make an appearance in vs. 4); presumably the poet wishes to identify himself and his priestly comrades with the chorus of IndraтАЩs associates, the Aс╣Еgirases, rather than with the god.
A brief grammatical digression is necessary here in order to show the particular artfulness of this hymn. As noted, the first three verses already describe, in some detail, the dawn and the sunrise, and so it might be thought that the sunrise in verse 10 is an anticlimax. But a remarkable fact about the first three verses is that the description of the sunrise there is couched almost entirely in the verb form known as the injunctive, which has no overt marker of tense. Although its default interpretation is past tense, it can be used also to depict тАЬtimelessтАЭ events. (Since English lacks such a verbal category, we have used the present tense here.) The sun rise in verses 1тАУ3 is both the mythic model of the Vala-Aс╣Еgiras narrative and, more important, the ideal sunrise to which the poet aspires. In contrast to the insistent injunctives in these verses, when todayтАЩs sunrise, the successful result of the sacri ficersтАЩ and poetтАЩs efforts, is depicted in verse 10, all four verb forms have the overt marker of past tense, the so-called augment, making it clear that the sunrise there has indeed (just) occurred. Another example of R╠еgvedic poetsтАЩ sensitivity to gram matical categories and their ingenious deployment of them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods On the structure of the hymn and the grammatical patterning that supports that structure, see published introduction. Note that this patterning imposes presential renderings of the injunctives in the first three vss.

рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рджрдпреЛ рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧреЛрдХреНрддрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рд╛рдВ рдкрдгрд┐рднрд┐рд░рдкрд╣реГрддреНрдп рдЧрд┐рд░реЗрд░рдзрдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░реЗрдг рд╡рд┐рдореЛрдХрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╡реЗрджрдпрджрд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ ред рдХрд┐рдореН ред рдЧрд╛ рдирд┐рдЧреВрдврд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН ред рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрджреНрд░рд┐рдВ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдиреН рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкрдиреН ред рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрд╛рдгрд╛рдореБрдкрд░рд┐ рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рднреЗрджрдирд╛рдп рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдиреН ред рдЖрдпрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЖрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдГ рдЕрд░реНрдЪрд┐рдирдГ рд░рд╢реНрдордпрдГ рдЧреБрдГ рдЕрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╕реГрддрд╛ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН ред рдЕрдкрд╛рд╡реГрдд рдЕрдкрд╛рд╡реГрдгреЛрддреН рд╡реНрд░рдЬрд┐рдиреАрдГ рддрдордГрдкреБрдЮреНрдЬрд╡рддреАрд░реНрдирд┐рд╢рд╛рдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓: рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдГ рдЙрддреН рдЧрд╛рддреН рдЙрджрдЧрд╛рддреН ред рддрдерд╛ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реАрдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреАрдГ рджреБрд░рдГ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐ рдЖрд╡рдГ рд╡реНрдпрд╡реГрдгреЛрддреН ред рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдкрдирдпрдиреЗрди рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдпрд╛рдХрд░реЛрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra) recovered (the hidden cattle), hurling his thunderbolt from heaven at the prayers of the Aс╣Еgirasas; the rays of the approaching dawn are spread around; the divine sun, scattering the clustered gloom, has risen and set open the doors of (the habitations of) men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Through knowledge unloosing the stone of heaven with hymnsтАФthe shining (beacons) of the approaching dawn come (out of it)тАФ
he uncloses (the doors) to the enclosures: the Sun comes up. The god has opened up the doors belonging to the sons of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Pp. interprets vid─Б╠Бas vid─Б╠Бс╕е, and this interpr. is followed by S─Бyaс╣Зa., Grassmann, Geldner, Renou (EVP XVI.107), and Witzel Got┼Н inter alia. It has the merit of providing a verb form for the opening p─Бda, but the 2nd sg. subjunctive it appears to be does not fit well in context. I prefer to take it as instr. sg. of the root noun v├нd- (vid─Б╠Бagainst the Pp.), as tentatively suggested by Oldenberg and, in different ways, adopted by L├╝ders (Varuс╣Зa 325), Thieme (rev. of L├╝ders, ZDMG 101 (1951) 417 [=KlSch 652]), Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 175- 76), and Hoffmann (Inj. 173-74). My interp. follows Hoffmann in particular in taking p─Бda b as parenthetical, with the singular verb appropriate to p─Бda a postponed until ├бp─Бvс╣Ыta in p─Бda c. I far prefer this solution to allowing the sg. part. viс╣гiy├бn in p─Бda a to be construed with the pl. phrase arc├нno guс╕е in b, with L├╝ders et al. The sg. subj.

of a,c is most likely the sun.

In b arc├нn- is interpr. either as тАШhaving chant, singingтАЩ (by most) or тАШhaving rays, brightтАЩ. Again with Hoffmann, I prefer the latter. Hoffmann (174 n. 125) suggests supplying ket├║- тАШbeamтАЩ, regularly associated with the dawns, and this seems contextually appropriate.

P─Бda c contains another -├нn-stem, this time a hapax, vraj├нn- тАШpossessing enclosuresтАЩ, in the fem. acc. pl.. Grassmann, Geldner, Hoffmann, and Witzel Got┼Н take the referent to be тАШcowsтАЩ, but the usual obj. of ├бpa тИЪvс╣Ы is the cow-enclosure (often the base of vraj├нn-, namely vraj├б-) or the doors thereto, and тАШdoorтАЩ is also fem. With Hoffmann and against the Pp. I take ├бp─Бvс╣Ыta as an injunc. ├бp─Б + vс╣Ыta.

The verb of d, v├н тАж ─Бvaс╕е, is undeniably augmented, however; I take it as a summary comment on the description found in the rest of the vs. See HoffmannтАЩs disc. 174-75.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sun distributes his radiance as it was a substance; the parent of the rays of light, (the dawn), knowing his approach, comes from the spacious (firmament); the rivers with running waters flow, breaking down their banks; the heaven is stable like a well-constructed pillar.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Sun unlooses his beauty like an ensign; the mother of the cows [=Dawn], recognizing (the way), comes here from the pen.
The rivers (of light) have floods (broad and high) like plains, have floods that chew (their banks). Heaven becomes firm like a
well-fixed pillar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ├бmati- see comm. ad I.73.2.

The problematic p─Бda is c. The rivers who are its subject are not, in my opinion, either real-world rivers (so, it seems, Geldner) or the heavenly streams so beloved of L├╝ders. Rather, to fit the context, they must be, metaphorically, the outpourings of light at dawn, which are so intense that they threaten to destabilize the world with their floods – a threat countered by the solidity of Heaven described in p─Бda d. The two bahuvr─лhis in c, dh├бnv-arс╣Зasaс╕е тАж kh─Б╠Бdo-arс╣З─Бс╕е, have been much discussed. Noteworthy first is the fact that they have (almost) the same final member: if both cmpds are nom. pl. the 2nd members are -arс╣Зas- and -arс╣Зa- respectively.

Thieme rejects the variation in stem, taking both as containing -arс╣Зas-, which requires the 2nd form to be nom. singular. In his interpr. the many rivers described by dh├бnvarс╣Зasaс╕е have joined into one, modified by singular kh─Б╠Бdoarс╣З─Бс╕е. It is a clever solution, but rather over-clever and in fact unnecessary. Both ├бrс╣Зas- and ├бrс╣Зa- exist independently, and the plural built to a cmpd. with ├бrс╣Зas- as final member (that is, - arс╣Зasaс╕е) would not fit a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, while one built to the parallel stem -arс╣Зadoes nicely, as if truncated from a Jagat─л cadence with -arс╣Зasaс╕е (see such a cadence in I.182.7).

What then do the cmpds mean? Again, a variety of interpr. have been suggested. I take dh├бnv-arс╣Зas- as an equational bv., тАШwhose floods are dh├бnu-тАЩ. A dh├бnu- appears to be a high flat plain or steppe; two of its five occurrences in the RV are characterized as bс╣Ыhat─л╠Б- тАШloftyтАЩ. In our context I think it refers to what we often call a тАЬwall of water,тАЭ a mass of oncoming water far above flood stage, perhaps already flooding over the banks and across the adjacent land. As for kh─Б╠Бdo-arс╣З─Бс╕е, it should mean something like тАШwhose floods are a biting/devouringтАЩ; in this case, I think Geldner (flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.) is correct that the rivers are devouring their banks, eating away at the solid ground. The sturdy pillar of heaven in d provides a bulwark against this featureless undulating torrent of light.

Griffith

Surya hath spread his light as splendour: hither came the Cows’ Mother, conscious, from the stable,
To streams that flow with biting waves to deserts; and heaven is stablished like a firm-set pillar.

Geldner

Surya entfaltete seine Pracht wie ein Bildnis; die Mutter der K├╝he kam des Weges kundig aus dem Verschlu├Я. Ihre Fluten ergie├Яen die Fl├╝sse, deren Fluten die Ufer anfressen. Der Himmel wurde gefestigt wie eine wohlaufgerichtete S├дule.

Grassmann

Wie Glanz erschloss die Sonne ihre Sch├╢nheit; vom Stall her kam der K├╝he Mutter kundig. Die Str├╢me wogten ├╝ber Fels und Ufer; der Himmel stand gleich wohlgesetzter S├дule.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo me, when offering praise, as to an ancient author of sacred songs, the burden of the cloud (descends); the cloud parts (with its burden); the sky performs (its office); he assiduously worshipping Aс╣Еgirasas are exhausted by much (adoration).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ancient author of sacred songs: mah─лn─Бm januс╣гe p┼лrvy─Бya = st┼лtin─Бm utp─Бdayitre pratnay─Б, to an ancient begetter or producer of praises; the cloud = the mountain, parvata

Jamison Brereton

In response to this hymn here the womb of the mountain (gapes open) for the primordial birth of the great ones [=dawns].
The mountain gapes open; heaven achieves success; desiring to win the earth, they [=poets/Aс╣Еgirases] exhaust themselves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. describes dawn as happening in response to and as a result of the hymn recited at this very moment (hence asma├н) at the dawn sacrifice. The two heavy dative phrases, polarized at both ends of the first hemistich, asm─Б╠Бukth─Б╠Бya and jan├║с╣гe p┼лrvy─Б╠Бya, have different functions in the clause. The gaping mountain is an allusion to the opening of the Vala cave, metaphorically applied to the advent of dawn from the night darkness.

In the second hemistich, in c тАЬheaven achieves successтАЭ must, in my view, allude to the successful emergence of dawnтАЩs light from the heavenly realm. This is contrasted with d, where an unnamed plural subject is desiring to win the earth (─Бv├нvasantaс╕е тАж bh┼л╠Бma) – in my opinion, this refers to the fact that features on the earth come only slowly to visual definition at dawn, even as the light comes streaming out of the sky. The unknown subjects are probably the poets responsible for тАЬthis hymn hereтАЭ (asm─Б╠Бukth─Б╠Бya) in p─Бda a; they must continue their verbal efforts, тАЬexhaust themselvesтАЭ (dasayanta), in order to bring the earth into focus.

Supplying тАШpoetsтАЩ as subj. generally follows Hoffmann, who thinks esp. of the Aс╣Еgirases (174 n. 126), contra Geldner, who takes bh┼л╠Бma as subj. (sim. L├╝ders). On dasayanta, see my -├бya-Formations, p. 59. Some take the verb rather to тИЪdaс╣Гs тАШwork wondersтАЩ; see esp. Thieme (loc. cit., n. 7), fld. by Schmidt, Witzel Got┼Н. This cannot be excluded, but I find the тАШexhaustтАЩ meaning more poetic compelling.

Griffith

This laud hath won the burden of the mountain. To aid the ancient birth of mighty waters
The mountain parted, Heaven performed his office. The worshippers were worn with constant serving.

Geldner

Vor diesem Loblied tat sich der Scho├Я des Berges auf zur ersten Geburt der gro├Яen Morgenr├╢ten. Der Berg tat sich auf, der Himmel ward hergestellt, die Erden ersch├╢pfen sich in Worten, um ihn herzubitten.

Grassmann

F├╝r diesen Spruch er├╢ffne sich des Berges, der grossen Fluten Schooss dem alten Stamme, Der Wolkenberg; sein Ziel erreich’ der Himmel, und die Verehrer beuten aus die Erde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI Indra and Agni, I invoke you for my salvation with well-uttered words, agreeable to the gods; for verily, sages excelling in sacrifice, and diligently adoring, worship you with sacred songs, prompt as the Maruts (in devotion).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With well-spoken words pleasing to the gods, Indra and Agni are now to be called upon by you for help,
for with solemn speeches sage poets of good sacrifice who desire to win always sacrifice to the Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vaс╕е in WackernagelтАЩs position can be construed in a number of different ways. I take it as the poetтАЩs address to his colleagues to praise and importune the two gods. Since the next two vss. (5-6) consist of 1st pl. exhortations to proceed with the sacrifice and achieve effective ritual poetry, my interpr. fits the larger context well.

Geldner also seems to assume the referents are human, but are rather the potential beneficiaries of the poetтАЩs own plea to the gods (sim. Witzel Got┼Н). By contrast Schmidt (and less clearly L├╝ders) take it as direct address to the gods; Schmidt тАЬтАж wollen wir jetzt euch, Indra und Agni, zur Hilfe rufen.тАЭ Given the number discrepancy between pl.

vaс╕е and the dual dvandva ├нndr─Б тАж agn─л╠Б, this seems unlikely. Note also that the noninitial accent on agn─л╠Бprecludes a voc. interpr. of the dvandva, though that alone would not prevent vaс╕е from referring to them.

I do not understand the intrusion of the Maruts here. They are not gods of the dawn sacrifice, nor are they associated with the Vala myth or with the Aс╣Еgirases.

Perhaps their prominence elsewhere in the Vth Maс╣Зс╕Нala (esp. V.52-61) is responsible for their brief appearance here, prompted by the mention of Indra. They are presumably not only the objects of y├бjanti but also of ─Бv├нvasantaс╕е: тАЬwinningтАЭ them would involve persuading them to come to our sacrifice.

Griffith

With hymns and God-loved words will I invoke you, Indra and Agni, to obtain your favour,
For verily sages, skilled in sacrificing, worship the Maruts and with lauds invite them.

Geldner

Mit wohlgesetzten, gottgef├дlligen Reden will ich jetzt Indra und Agni f├╝r euch zur Gnade anrufen, denn mit Lobliedern verehren die Weisen unter sch├╢nen Opfern die Marut, um sie herzubitten.

Grassmann

Zu H├╝lfe ruft nun Indra her und Agni durch eure sch├╢nen, gottgef├дll’gen Spr├╝che; Denn unter Spr├╝chen opfern auch die Weisen mit sch├╢nen Opfern huldigend den Maruts.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome today quickly; let us be engaged in pious acts; let us entirely annihilate the hostile; let us keep off all sacred enemies; let us hasten to the presence of the instrumental tutor of the rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Come on now! Today let us become possessed of good poetic vision. Let us send misfortune forth a wide way away.
Let us put hatreds aside in the distance; let us go forward to the
sacrificer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As suggested already by Geldner (n. 5b) and, independently, Thieme (ZDMG 95 [1941] 82-83 [=KlSch. 7-8]) and accepted by all subsequent tr., a better reading is obtained by segmenting duch├║n─Бm inav─Бma, against Pp. duch├║n─Б minav─Бma. This requires no emendation to the Saс╣Гhit─Б text.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these two vss. form an omphalos and are structurally parallel, with the poet addressing his priest-poet colleagues with hortatory subjunctives. The immediacy of the vss. and the sacrificial context of the hymn make this a more likely scenario than S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs suggestion that the Aс╣Еgirases are speaking these vss. For strenuous arguments against S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs interpr., see L├╝ders p. 327.

Griffith

This day approach us: may our thoughts be holy, far from us let us cast away misfortune.
Let us keep those who hate us at a distance, and haste to meet the man who sacrifices.

Geldner

Wohlan! Wir wollen heute gute Gedanken hegen und die unheilvollen Absichten verbannen. Die Feindschaft wollen wir weit fortschaffen und bereitwillig zu dem Opfernden kommen.

Kommt heute her, wir wollen sein voll Andacht, wir wollen weithin jagen die Unholden, In weite Ferne unsre Hasser setzen, und vorw├дrts eilen hin zu dem, der opfert.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome, friends, let us celebrate that solemn rite which was effectual in setting open the (secret) stalls of the (stolen) cattle; by which Manu overcame Vi┼Ыi┼Ыipra; by which the merchant, going to the wood (for it), obtained the water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vi┼Ыisipra: manur vi┼Ыisipram jig─Бya = Manu conquered the enemy without a chin, or as ┼Ыipra means also a nose, it might mean noseless; Indra and Vс╣Ыtra may be here intended; by which the merchant: vaс╣Зij vaс╣Еkur ─Бp─Б pur─лс╣гam: an allusion to the legend of kakс╣г─лv─Бn

Jamison Brereton

Come on! Comrades, let us create (the same) poetic vision with which the mother opened the enclosure of the cow,
with which Manu conquered Vi┼Ыi┼Ыipra, with which the wandering
merchant reached the overflowing source (of goods?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unlike the first hortatory vs., this second one is not entirely tied to the hereand-now; rather it provides three separate historical/mythological models for the effective poetic vision (dh─л╠Б-) that we are aiming to create now (p─Бda a). The first model (b) appears to be a variant of the Vala myth so prominent in the rest of the hymn, but those in c and d are obscure.

In b the first question is the grammatical identity of y─Б╠Б. It is generally taken as nom. sg. fem., but Oldenberg suggests that it might alternatively be a (short) instr. sg. fem.

In the former case the referent of y─Б╠Бwould be the dh─л╠Б- of p─Бda a, which would be the subj. of с╣Ыс╣Зuta and identified with the тАЬmother of the cowтАЭ (m─Бt─Б╠БтАж g├│с╕е); in the latter it would be parallel to the two instr. sg. fem. y├бy─Б opening c and d. I favor the second interpr.; although the former is not impossible, I find the syntactic parallelism a stronger argument, and y─Б╠Бcould owe its abbreviated form to being displaced from initial position by the preverb ├бpa. If the instr. interpr. is correct, this leaves the subj.

of с╣Ыс╣Зuta and referent of тАЬmother of the cowтАЭ open. Oldenberg and Geldner both consider it to be Uс╣гas. Again, this is not impossible, but I think it may be Saram─Б, whose finding of the cows is treated in vss. 7-8 – though Dawn as тАЬmother of cowsтАЭ (g├бv─Бm m─Бt─Б╠Б) is found in vs. 2 and is also a strong candidate.

Geldner remarks apopos of p─Бda c тАЬsonst unbekannte SageтАЭ (see also L├╝ders, p. 329), and it is likely that we will not get further than that. Ad VII.99.4 Oldenberg tentatively suggests that the name of a D─Бsa, vс╣Ыс╣гa┼Ыipr├б, that occurs in that passage might have something to do with our vi┼Ыi┼Ыipr├б-, but even if so (and itтАЩs certainly possible), this is a deadend, since all we know of Vс╣Ыс╣гa┼Ыipra is that heтАЩs a D─Бsa and killed by Indra and Viс╣гс╣Зu. Like the Maruts in 4d, the fleeting intrusion of Manu here is unexpected and unexplained.

Even more so the тАЬwandering merchantтАЭ (vaс╣З├нg vaс╣Еk├║с╕е) of d. On vaс╣Еk├║- see comm. ad I.51.11 and, esp., I.114.4. Although the standard rendering is тАШflyingтАЩ (see, e.g., Geldner, Schmidt), its derivation from тИЪva├▒c тАШmove crookedly, meanderтАЩ makes тАШmeandering, wanderingтАЩ more likely. In I.114.4 it modifies kav├н-. I suggest there that it refers to an itinerant poet, and merchants are at least as likely as poets to be itinerant, following a meandering course as they peddle their goods. But who this particular merchant is meant to be and how and why he needs a dh─л╠Б- to attain his p┼л╠Бr─лс╣гa- remain unclear. If I had Dum├йzilian tendencies, I might suggest a trifunctional interpr.: p─Бda b = 1st function, c = 2nd function, and d = 3rd function (at least the latter two might work – 1st

-function b is a bit of a stretch). But even if this interpr. were persuasive, it doesnтАЩt explain what the material is doing in this hymn at this point.

05-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these two vss. form an omphalos and are structurally parallel, with the poet addressing his priest-poet colleagues with hortatory subjunctives. The immediacy of the vss. and the sacrificial context of the hymn make this a more likely scenario than S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs suggestion that the Aс╣Еgirases are speaking these vss. For strenuous arguments against S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs interpr., see L├╝ders p. 327.

Griffith

Come, let us carry out, O friends, the purpose wherewith the Mother threw the Cow’s stall open,
That wherewith Manu conquered Visisipra, wherewith the wandering merchant gained heaven’s water.

Geldner

Wohlan! Wir wollen das Gebet verrichten, ihr Freunde, durch das die Mutter den Pferch der Kuh aufschlo├Я, durch das Manu den Visisipra besiegte, durch das der fliegende Kaufmann den Quell erlangte.

Grassmann

Kommt, Freunde, her, lasst uns Gebet verrichten, durch das die Mutter sich erschloss den Kuhstall, Durch das einst Manu schlug den Vi├зi├зipra, durch das der rege H├дndler Nass erlangte.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt this sacrifice the stone (set in motion) by the hands (of the priests) makes a noise, whereby the nine-months ministrants celebrated the ten-months worship; when Saram─Б, going to the ceremony, discovered the cattle, and Aс╣Еgiras rendered all the rites effective.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ten-months worship: or, when the priests of both the nine and ten months rites offered worship;

Saram─Б: may signify either flowing, eulogistic, or sacred speech, ┼Ыaraс╣Зa┼Ы─лl─Б stutir┼лpa v─Бk, or, as usual, the bitch of Indra

Jamison Brereton

The (pressing) stone, guided by the hand, bellowed there, the stone along with which the Navagvas sang for ten months.
Saram─Б, going after the truth, found the cows; the Aс╣Еgiras made all things real.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note that 3 of the 4 verbs are augmented (├бn┼лnot, ─Б╠Бrcan, avindat), the 4th a preterital pf. (cak─Бra).

07-08 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the mythic model of the dawn accompanying the dawn ritual, the opening of the Vala cave through the verbal efforts of the Aс╣Еgirases, is spelled out. Note the variant versions of the phrase тАЬSaram─Б found the cowsтАЭ: 7c sar├бm─Б g─Б╠Бavindat, with augmented imperfect; 8d sar├бm─Б vidad g─Б╠Бс╕е, with aor. injunctive (per Pp.) or aor. indicative (sar├бm─Бvidad, with augmented avidat is a possible reading). For HoffmannтАЩs interpr. of this vs. pair see Injunk. 164-65.

Griffith

Here, urged by hands, loudly hath rung the press-stone wherewith Navagvas through ten months sang praises.
Sarama went aright and found the cattle. Angiras gave effect to all their labours.

Geldner

Es br├╝llte dabei der mit der Hand regierte Pre├Яstein, mit dem die Navagva┬┤s zehn Monate lang den G├╢ttern lobsangen. Sarama ging den rechten Weg und fand die K├╝he. Alles hat der Angiras wahrgemacht.

Grassmann

Da t├╢nte laut der handgelenkte Pressstein, mit dem zehn Monde lang die Neuner sangen, Auf rechtem Pfad fand Sarama die K├╝he, und alles machte wahr der Angirase.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen all the Aс╣Еgirasas, on the opening of this adorable dawn, came in contact with the (discovered) cattle, then milk and the rest were offered in the august assembly, for Saram─Б had found cows by the path of truth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When all the Aс╣Еgirases roared along with the cows at the brightening of this great (dawn),
at the fountainhead of them [=cows], in the highest seat, Saram─Б found the cows along the path of truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The subordinator y├бd comes quite late (2nd position p─Бda b) in the subordinate clause presumably occupying the first hemistich, and it is preceded not only by the subj. (v├н┼Ыve) but by a heavy temporal loc. expression (asy─Б╠Бvy├║с╣гi m─Б╠Бhin─Бy─Бс╕е) – in violation of standard RVic subordinator placement. This anomaly may have led Witzel Got┼Н to take p─Бda a as a nominal main clause: тАЬSie alle (waren) тАж (zugegen).тАЭ I am sympathetic, but think the clause division is unnecessarily radical.

It is possible that b is a conversion into a subordinate clause of IV.3.11b s├бm ├бс╣Еgiraso navanta g├│bhiс╕е with p─Бda a acting as a preposed afterthought.

The 2nd hemistich brings another syntactic problem: in c the Pp. interprets ├║tsa (before a vowel) as nom. -aс╕е, a grammatical ident. that in turn requires that c be an independent clause. The Pp. reading is defended by Oldenberg and fld. by many, incl. Geldner, Hoffmann (Injunk. 165), Witzel Got┼Н. With L├╝ders (385 n. 2; fld. by Schmidt p. 177, Janert p.

  1. I prefer the loc. ├║tse, parallel to param├й sadh├бsthe, and defining the place where Saram─Б found the cows in d.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the mythic model of the dawn accompanying the dawn ritual, the opening of the Vala cave through the verbal efforts of the Aс╣Еgirases, is spelled out. Note the variant versions of the phrase тАЬSaram─Б found the cowsтАЭ: 7c sar├бm─Б g─Б╠Бavindat, with augmented imperfect; 8d sar├бm─Б vidad g─Б╠Бс╕е, with aor. injunctive (per Pp.) or aor. indicative (sar├бm─Бvidad, with augmented avidat is a possible reading). For HoffmannтАЩs interpr. of this vs. pair see Injunk. 164-65.

Griffith

When at the dawning of this mighty Goddess, Angirases all sang forth with the cattle,-
Their spring is in the loftiest place of meeting,-Sarama found the kine by Order’s pathway.

Als bei dem Aufleuchten dieser Herrlichkeiten alle Angirasen in das Gebr├╝ll der K├╝he einstimmten, da war ihr Quell am fernsten Ort. Auf dem rechten Wege fand Sarama die K├╝he.

Grassmann

Als da bei dieser grossen G├╢ttin Leuchten die Angirasen mit den K├╝hen br├╝llten, Fand Sarama am h├╢chsten Ort die K├╝he an deren Quelle auf dem Pfad des Rechtes.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay S┼лrya, lord of seven steeds, arrive, for he has a distant goal (to reach) by a tedious route; fleet as a hawk he pounces upon the offered (sacrificial) food; ever young and far-seeing, he shines, moving amidst rays of light.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the Sun drive here with his seven horses to the tract of land
stretching widely at (the end of) his long course.
Let the quick falcon fly to the stalk and the youthful poet shine as he goes among the cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is metrically problematic. Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition put the p─Бda break after sapt─Б╠Б┼Ыvaс╕е and distract s┼л╠Бryo, y─Бtu, and sapt─Б╠Б┼Ыvaс╕е; their 2nd p─Бda, beginning kс╣г├йtram, has a caesura after 3 (though see their n.). It is also possible to take kс╣г├йtram as the last word of p─Бda a (see SchmidtтАЩs layout, p. 178) and to restrict the distraction to a single word, either s┼л╠Бryaс╕е or sapt─Б╠Б┼Ыvaс╕е, though this produces a bad cadence. In that case I would suggest that the 2nd p─Бda orig. began *y├бd y├бd; reading *y├бd y├бd asya produces an opening of 4 and, with post-caesura urviy─Б╠Бd─лrgay─Бth├й, makes a fine Triс╣гс╣нubh. The 2nd (or 1st) y├бd would be the neut. sg. N/A participle to тИЪi.

Even if this possible emendation is not accepted, it is still possible to take y├бd as the neut. participle, not the subordinator: this interpr. is represented in my tr. by тАЬstretchingтАЭ and by the lack of a relative cl. With double y├бd the tr. would read тАЬto the tract of land which is stretching widely at (the end of) his long course.тАЭ The 2nd hemistich contains a pres. injunctive, patayat, and a pf. [/redupl. pres.] subjunctive d─лdayat. In the published translation they are both rendered as imperatives, matching the pattern set by y─Бtu in p─Бda a. I now think that this interpr. lacks refinement and should be altered. The vs. in general concerns the coincidence between the sunrise and the ritual activities of the dawn sacrifice. We hope for the sunrise (hence the impv.), which is in fact realized in the next vs. By contrast, the ritual activities in the 2nd hemistich are under our (=priestsтАЩ) control and can therefore simply be described.

Exactly what the referents of the falcon (c) and the young poet (d) are is disputed (see the various interpr., incl. those that do not consider them ritual referents at all [notably L├╝ders 329-31]). Starting with d, y├║van- kav├н- is frequently an epithet of Agni and тИЪd─л is a typical Agni verb, so it seems likely that this is a reference to the kindling of the fire at the dawn ritual. Although тАЬgoing among the cowsтАЭ sounds more like soma (mixing with milk), the cows here can be the ghee oblations poured into the fire, which will cause it to flame more brightly. If d refers to Agni, then c is likely to refer to Soma; certainly the ├бndhas- тАШstalkтАЩ is Soma vocabulary, and the falcon is SomaтАЩs vehicle in the Somaraub. What exactly is going on eludes me, however. As for the tense/mood distinction between patayat and d─лdayat, it may be that the distinction is illusory: one of them was simply brought into superficial harmony with the other, so that both end in -ayat, though they should be inj. and subj.

respectively. Or it may be that the injunc. is followed by a subj. to indicate that the 2nd action follows the first (тАЬthe falcon flies to the stalk; the young poet will shine тАжтАЭ).

Griffith

Borne by his Coursers Seven may Surya visit the field that spreadeth wide for his long journey.
Down on the Soma swooped the rapid Falcon. Bright was the young Sage moving mid his cattle.

Geldner

Der Sonnengott mit sieben Rossen soll zu dem Gefilde kommen, das auf seiner langen Fahrt sich weithin erstreckt. Der rasche Falke fliege zum Somatrunk; der jugendliche Seher erstrahle, wenn er auf die K├╝he ausgeht.

Grassmann

Mit sieben Rossen komme her die Sonne zum Feld, das weit auf ihrer Bahn sich hinstreckt, Der schnelle Adler fliege hin zum Soma; zu K├╝hen eilend strahl’ der junge Seher.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬS┼лrya has ascended above the glistening water, as soon as he has put to his bright-backed steeds; sage (worshippers) have drawn him, like a ship, across the sea; the waters hearing his commands, have come down.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S┼лrya has ascended: s┼лryo aruhat ┼Ыukram arс╣Зas = s┼лrya has mounted the bright water, that is, he has become everywhere visible, but it may be an allusion to the sun’s rising apparently out of the sea

Jamison Brereton

The Sun has mounted the gleaming flood, now that he has yoked his golden, straight-backed (horses).
Like a boat through the water the wise ones guided him; the waters,
giving heed, stood still nearby.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The structure of this vs. matches that of the last one: the first half describes a cosmic event outside of human control; the second ascribes control to the ritualists.

What is striking is that the same event is treated in both halves: the rising of the sun.

In ab the Sun has agency; he yoked his own horses and mounted the sky. But in c it is the priest-poets (тАЬthe wiseтАЭ dh─л╠Бr─Бс╕е) who guide him, through the waters that stand still for this progress, тАЬgiving heedтАЭ (─Б┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зvant─л╠Бс╕е) presumably to the poetsтАЩ words. (I owe the germ of this interpr. to Dieter Gunkel [p.c.].)

Griffith

Surya hath mounted to the shining ocean when he hath yoked his fair-backed Tawny Horses.
The wise have drawn him like a ship through water: the floods obedient have descended hither.

Geldner

Surya hat jetzt das lichte Meer erstiegen, da er die geradr├╝ckigen Falbinnen angesschirrt hat. Die Verst├дndigen lenkten ihn wie ein Schiff durchs Wasser. In der N├дhe zuh├╢rend standen die Gew├дsser still.

Grassmann

Der Sonnengott stieg auf zum hellen Luftmeer, als er geschirrt die blonden, glatten Stuten; Die klugen fuhren wie das Schiff im Meer ihn, und lauschend standen nah dabei die Wasser.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдзрд┐рдпрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдореН рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ рдЕрдмреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддреНрд░реАрдВ рджрдзрд┐рд╖реЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд╛рдорд┐ рее рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдордзреНрдпрдордГ рее рдпрдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рдирд╡рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рдГ рджрд╢ рдорд╛рд╕рдГ рдЕрддрд░рдиреН рд╕рддреНрд░рдордиреБрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрдГ рдЕрдпрд╛ рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ рджреЗрд╡реИрд░реНрдЧреБрдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рднрд╡реЗрдо ред рдЕрдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЕрдВрд╣: рдкрд╛рдкрдореН рдЕрддрд┐ рддреБрддреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо рдЕрддрд┐рддрд░реЗрдо рее рее реирен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI offer to you, (gods), for the sake of water, an all-bestowing sacrifice, whereby the nine-months ministrants have completed the ten-months rite; may we, by this sacrifice, be the protected of the gods; may we, by this sacrifice, cross over the boundaries of sin.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You have acquired the poetic vision that wins the sun in the waters, with which the Navagvas passed ten months.
Through this vision may we be those who have gods as our herdsmen; through this vision may we pass beyond constraint.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most interpr. construe aps├║ with dadhiс╣гe and tr. the latter as тАШyou have placedтАЩ, hence тАЬyou have placed your dh─л╠Бin the waters.тАЭ But med. forms of тИЪdh─Б generally mean тАШacquire, assumeтАЩ, and furthermore the standard interpr. is either nonsensical or requires a substantial backstory – such as OldenbergтАЩs тАЬ[ein] Zauber f├╝r Wiedererscheinen der Sonne nach langen Regeng├╝ssen.тАЭ I follow Geldner in taking aps├║ with svarс╣г─Б╠Бm тАЬdas тАж die Sonne im Wasser gewinntтАЭ; the sun was manifestly in the water(s) in the immediately preceding vs. – however metaphorically we wish to interpret those waters (I would take them as the floods of dawn light we encountered in vs. 2). Thus тАЬwinning the sun in the watersтАЭ is simply an expression for causing the sun to rise at dawn. For further disc. on the place of this vs. in the hymn, see published

introduction.

The number discrepancy between 2nd pl. vaс╕е and 2nd sg. dadhiс╣гe is easily accounted for in the same general manner as the vaс╕е in vs. 4 (see comm. thereon): dadhiс╣гe is the poetтАЩs self-address to himself, while vaс╕е is addressed to his colleagues.

As in vss. 5-6, these two distinct 2nd ps. references are joined in a joint 1st pl. in cd (sy─Бma тАж tutury─Бma).

Griffith

I lay upon the Floods your hymn, lightwinning, wherewith Navagvas their ten months completed.
Through this our hymn may we have Gods to guard us: through this our hymn pass safe beyond affliction.

Geldner

Du hast das Gebet verrichtet, das f├╝r euch die Sonne im Wasser gewinnt, mit dem die Navagva┬┤s die zehn Monate ausdauerten. Durch dieses Gebet wollen wir gottbeh├╝tet sein, durch dieses Gebet wollen wir die Not ├╝berdauern.

Grassmann

Eu’r Lied, was Licht schafft, gabest du den Wassern, durch das die Neuner zehn der Monde f├╝llten; Durch dies Gebet lasst sein uns Gott-beschirmet, durch dies Gebet lasst Noth uns ├╝berwinden.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреА рдпрд╛рдЪрдирд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! (рдпрдпрд╛) рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рдирд╡рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдирд╡реАрди рдЧрдордирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рджрд╢) рджрд╢ (рдорд╛рд╕рдГ) рдорд╣реАрдиреЗ (рдЕрддрд░рдиреН) рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рдЕрдпрд╛) рдЗрд╕ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рджреЗрд╡рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЕрдпрд╛) рдЗрд╕ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ) рдкрд╛рдк рд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рдк рд╕реЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рджреБрдГрдЦ рдХрд╛ (рдЕрддрд┐, рддреБрддреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реЗрдВ (рд╡рдГ) рдЖрдкрдХреА (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЙрд╕ (рдзрд┐рдпрдореН) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдореИрдВ (рджрдзрд┐рд╖реЗ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реВрдБ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН, рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рдмрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕рдм рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рджреБрдГрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдкреИрдВрддрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕рддреНрддрд╛рдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдпрд╛ рдирд╡рдЧреНрд╡рд╛ рджрд╢ рдорд╛рд╕реЛрд╜рддрд░рдиреНрдирдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рджреЗрд╡рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╜рдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рдВрд╜рд╣реЛрд╜рддрд┐ рддреБрддреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдВ рдзрд┐рдпрдордкреНрд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╣рдВ рджрдзрд┐рд╖реЗ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдзрд┐рдпрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╛ (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ) (рджрдзрд┐рд╖реЗ) рдзрд╛рд░рдпреЗрдпрдореН (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдореН) рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рд╕рдирддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬрддрд┐ рдпрдпрд╛ рддрд╛рдореН (рдпрдпрд╛) (рдЕрддрд░рдиреН) рддрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ (рджрд╢) (рдорд╛рд╕рдГ) (рдирд╡рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдирд╡реАрдирдЧрддрдпрдГ (рдЕрдпрд╛) рдЕрдирдпрд╛ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рджреЗрд╡рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ) рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдпрд╛) (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) (рддреБрддреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпреЗрдо (рдЕрддрд┐) (рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ) рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдкрд╛рдкрдЬрдиреНрдпрдВ рджреБрдГрдЦрдВ рд╡рд╛ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рдзреАрдордиреНрддреЛ рдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдмрд▓рд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рддрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рди, рдзрдирд╡рд╛рди рд╡ рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рди рдмрдиреВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рддреВрди рддрд░реВрди рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
